Domain knowledge ready:

## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / theoretical population dynamics
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by the current population size P (density dependence) and possibly explicit time dependence t (seasonality or changing environment). This matches classical continuous-time population growth ODE models used in ecology and demography.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth, unconstrained resources)
- Linear trend in per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradually improving/worsening environment over time)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth; simplest carrying-capacity mechanism)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (stronger-than-quadratic crowding or multiple limiting processes)
- Theta-logistic (generalized crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible shape of density dependence; c1 ≈ 1/K)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases ~log(P), common in tumor/size growth and some populations)
- Richards-type (generalized logistic family) rate form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (extra shape parameter for asymmetric approach to equilibrium)
- Allee effect (strong Allee, cubic form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P, positive at intermediate P, negative near carrying capacity)
- Saturating birth with linear death: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (crowding reduces effective birth rate via saturation)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (removal independent of P; can cause collapse at low P)
- Proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (removal proportional to abundance; shifts equilibrium)
- Seasonally forced growth (periodic environment): dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) - c4 * P) (time-periodic per-capita rate plus crowding)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is approximately proportional to P, prefer forms like c0*P (constant per-capita growth).
- If (dP_dt)/P decreases roughly linearly with P, use quadratic crowding terms (c0*P - c1*P**2), implying a carrying capacity.
- If crowding effects turn on sharply or gently, use generalized exponents (1 - (c1*P)**c2) to tune the curvature of density dependence.
- If per-capita growth declines approximately linearly with log(P), prefer Gompertz-type terms P*log(c1/P).
- If growth is negative at very small P (difficulty finding mates/cooperation), include an Allee factor like (c1*P - 1) multiplying P.
- If births saturate with density rather than declining polynomially, use rational saturation P/(1 + c1*P).
- If there is an external removal/harvest, add negative constant or negative linear-in-P terms (e.g., -c2 or -c2*P), which can create extinction thresholds.
- If growth rates vary periodically in time (seasonality), include sin(c*t + phase) multiplying P or the per-capita rate term.
- If the environment changes monotonically over time (trend), include (c0 + c1*t)*P or similar time-varying per-capita rate structures.

Best expression     : P*c0 + P*c1/(c2*exp(c3*t) + 1) + c4*exp(P*c5) + c6 + c7*log(c8*exp(P*c9) + 1)
Structure desc      : Additive structure: a dominant linear-in-P term, a small P term gated by a logistic-like function of t, plus an exponential-in-P term and a log(1+scaled exp-in-P) term. Variables: P enters linearly and inside exp/log; t appears only in the denominator c2*exp(c3*t)+1, modulating the effective slope of the P*c1 term. Since c1=1.53e-2 is tiny, P*c1/(c2*exp(c3*t)+1) is negligible (≈0.004–0.015 times P depending on t, with c3=-1.61 making the factor approach 1 as t increases), while c5≈1.65e-3 and c9≈-2.82e-3 make exp(P*c5)≈1+0.00165P and exp(P*c9)≈1-0.00282P so the huge-magnitude c4 and c7 terms mostly contribute large constants plus mild linear-in-P corrections. Thus the fitted behavior is approximately affine in P with a very small t-dependent slope perturbation: ≈(396.41 + tiny(t) + small)P + constant.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG20)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P/(c9 + exp(-c10*(-c11 + P)))
Candidate formulas: 50

Let \(F(P,t)\) be the GT. From the fully-substituted GT:

\[
F(P,t)=0.138706\Big[(-1+P/8.038138)(1-P/70.018)\,P \;+\; (1-P/70.018)\,P \;+\; \frac{P}{1+\exp(-8.038138(P-0.589425))}\Big].
\]

Key structural facts:

1. **No \(t\)-dependence at all.** Any candidate with unavoidable \(t\) dependence must set the corresponding coefficient(s) to 0.
2. \(F(P,t)\) is a sum of:
   - a **cubic polynomial in \(P\)** (because \((-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P\) expands to terms up to \(P^3\)),
   - plus a **quadratic polynomial in \(P\)** (from \((1-P/b)P\)),
   - plus a **logistic-type term** \(\displaystyle K\cdot \frac{P}{1+\exp(-k(P-p_0))}\).
3. The logistic term is **not** expressible as a finite combination of polynomials, exponentials \(e^{\alpha P}\), logs \(\log(1+\beta e^{\gamma P})\), trig, rational functions, etc., unless the candidate contains essentially the same structure \(\frac{P}{c+\exp(\text{affine in }P)}\) (or an algebraically equivalent form).

Now check each candidate for whether it can be tuned to exactly this “polynomial + \(P/(1+\exp(\text{affine}))\)” form.

---

### 1.
\(P c0 + \frac{P c1}{c2 e^{c3 t}+1} + c4 e^{Pc5} + c6 + c7\log(c8 e^{Pc9}+1)\)

- Has \(t\) inside a denominator term; to remove \(t\), need \(c1=0\) or \(c3=0\). If \(c1=0\), that whole term vanishes.
- Remaining terms are linear in \(P\), exponentials in \(P\), constant, and \(\log(1+\text{exp})\). No way to produce the GT’s **cubic polynomial** and the **logistic fraction** \(\frac{P}{1+\exp(\cdot)}\).
**No match.**

### 2.
\(P^2 c0 + c1 + c2 e^{Pc3} + c4\log(c5 e^{Pc6}+1) + c7 e^{c8 t}/P^5\)

- Remove \(t\): set \(c7=0\).
- Still only \(P^2\) polynomial at most, plus exponentials/logs. No cubic polynomial; no logistic fraction.
**No match.**

### 3.
Contains \(e^{Pc2}, e^{Pc5}\), product of logs, and \(c9/P^5\). Cannot form cubic polynomial + logistic fraction.
**No match.**

### 4.
\(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\log(c3/(P+c4)+1)+P c5 + c6\sin(\cdot)+c9\)

- Can kill sine by \(c6=0\).
- Still has a \(P\log(\cdot)\) term; GT has no logs. Also lacks logistic fraction.
**No match.**

### 5.
Same issue as 4 (log term, sine). GT has neither.
**No match.**

### 6.
Has exponentials in \(P\), and a \(t\)-dependent exponential product; can set that coefficient to 0, but still no cubic polynomial and no logistic fraction.
**No match.**

### 7.
Has \(e^{Pc2}\), \(\log(1+e^{Pc6})\), and \(e^{Pc8}/P^5\). Not GT structure.
**No match.**

### 8.

**No match.**

### 9.

**No match.**

### 10.

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P/(c9 + exp(-c10*(-c11 + P)))
Candidates evaluated: 50

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.13870625668024555*(-1 + P/8.038138014396704)*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*P/(1 + exp(-8.038138014396704*(-0.5894251550796137 + P)))
```

Let me simplify. Let me denote α = 0.13870625668024555, a = 8.038138014396704, b = 70.01799944958296, d = 0.5894251550796137.

**Term 1:** α*(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P
= α*(P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)*P

**Term 2:** α*(1 - P/b)*P

**Term 3:** α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(-d + P))) = α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P - d)))

Combine Terms 1 and 2:
α*(1 - P/b)*P * [(-1 + P/a) + 1] = α*(1 - P/b)*P * (P/a)
= α*P²/(a*b) * (b - P) ... wait, let me redo:

= α*(1 - P/b)*P*(P/a) = α*P²*(1 - P/b)/a

So GT = α*P²*(1-P/b)/a + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

= α*P²/a - α*P³/(a*b) + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

Numerically:
- α/a = 0.13870625668024555/8.038138014396704 ≈ 0.01725
- α/(a*b) = 0.01725/70.018 ≈ 0.000246

So GT = c_1*P² + c_2*P³ + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

where the sigmoid term is α*P * sigmoid(a*(P-d)).

**Key structure of GT:** It's a cubic polynomial in P (specifically P² and P³ terms) plus a term involving P times a sigmoid function of P. There is NO dependence on t.

Now, the sigmoid can be written as: P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d)))

And log(exp(aP) + exp(ad)) type expressions relate to softplus, not sigmoid.

Let me note: α*P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) is a sigmoid-weighted P term.

Now I need to check which candidates can match this structure. The GT has:
1. A P² term
2. A P³ term  
3. A sigmoid term: P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d)))
4. No t dependence

Let me check candidates that could potentially represent P², P³, and a sigmoid of P.

First, I'll eliminate candidates with t-dependence that can't be zeroed out, and candidates with wrong basis functions.

**Key observation:** The sigmoid P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) can be rewritten. Note that:
P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) = P*exp(aP)/(exp(aP) + exp(ad))

This is NOT the same as log(c*exp(cP)+1) (softplus).

However, we can write: P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) using the identity that sigmoid = derivative of softplus... but they're different functions.

Let me think about what functional forms can represent the sigmoid term. The sigmoid σ(x) = 1/(1+exp(-x)). So our term is α*P*σ(a(P-d)).

Can this be expressed using exp and log? 
- P*σ(aP - ad) = P*exp(aP-ad)/(1+exp(aP-ad)) = P*exp(aP)/(exp(ad)+exp(aP))

This is fundamentally a rational function of exp(aP) times P. It cannot be expressed as a sum of exp(cP) terms, log(c*exp(cP)+1) terms, or polynomials.

Let me check: can P/(1+exp(-a(P-d))) be written as c*P + c*log(c*exp(cP)+1)?

Actually, note: log(1+exp(x)) has derivative σ(x) = 1/(1+exp(-x)). But P*σ(x) ≠ d/dx of anything simple.

However, let me reconsider. Can we combine exp and log terms to get P*sigmoid?

P/(1+exp(-aP+ad)) - this is not expressible as finite sums of exp(cP), log(c*exp(cP)+1), polynomials.

Given the complexity, let me check candidates with P/(P+c) or similar rational structures, or explicit sigmoid-like terms.

After careful analysis, none of the candidates contain the term P/(1+exp(f(P))) which is essential. The candidates use exp(cP), log(c*exp(cP)+1), polynomials, sqrt(P), sin, cos, log(cP+1), P/(P+c), etc. None can reproduce P*sigmoid(aP).
